         <div class="mosaic-container Pos-r W-100 BgColor-Body" data-animation-state="2" style="min-height:100vh;z-index:8;background-color:#f2f2f2;">

            </a>

          <div class="Pos-r Z-0 article-container" data-template="desktop" id="article-105025103717" style="background-color:white;min-height:315px;">
           <div class="Pos-r sticky-container print-article" style="min-height:315px;">
            <div class="article-inner-container" style="max-width:1280px;">
             <div class="inset-container Mx-a">
              <div class="GridTable">
               <div class="D-tbr row-template">
                <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left">
                 <div class="content" style="width:825px;min-width:825px;">

                   <div class="D-tbr row-content">
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left Pend-20" style="width:305px;max-width:305px;">
                     <h1 class="Font-A-6-110 title W-100" id="article-aft-title-105025103717">
                      Dad Faces 20 Years for Cheating Harvard Financial Aid
                     </h1>
                     <div class="attribution-component D-b W-100" id="article-aft-attribution-105025103717" style="max-width:305px;">
                      <div class="author-info author-info-text-first Pt-10 W-100 Bd-t Bd-b Bdstart-0 Bdend-0">
                       <div class="GridTable W-100">
                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t">
                          <cite class="D-b Fs-n Pb-14 byline col">
                           <span class="D-b author-name col-left">
                            <a class="Font-C-2-140 Fw-b" data-action-outcome="navigate" data-routable-url="/parenting/author/jennifer-o'neill" data-ylk="t1:a2;t2:article;t3:cat;t8:3692d62e-e626-3217-821c-8230d2a0d04f;t9:16;elm:itm;elmt:cat;itc:0" href="/parenting/author/jennifer-o'neill" rel="author" style="color:#000;">
                             Jennifer O'Neill
                            </a>
                           </span>
                           <span class="D-b Font-C-2-140 Fw-n author-title">
                            Writer
                           </span>
                           <time class="D-b Font-C-2-140 Fw-n date">
                            <span>
                             December 12, 2014
                            </span>
                           </time>
                           <div class="follow Mt-4">
                            <iframe allowtransparency="true" frameborder="0" scrolling="no" src="//platform.twitter.com/widgets/follow_button.html?screen_name=JONEILL2010&amp;show_screen_name=false&amp;show_count=false" style="border:none;overflow:hidden;width:60px;height:20px;">
                            </iframe>
                           </div>
                          </cite>
                         </div>
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t Va-b" style="width:133px;">
                          <a class="attribution-photo author-photo-link col" data-action-outcome="navigate" data-routable-url="/parenting/author/jennifer-o'neill" data-ylk="t1:a2;t2:article;t3:cat;t8:3692d62e-e626-3217-821c-8230d2a0d04f;t9:16;elm:itm;elmt:cat;itc:0" href="/parenting/author/jennifer-o'neill">
                           <img alt="Jennifer O'Neill" class="author-photo" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w133/4c3da7d2f8a668f9d3d45d4c2c0a68ddec512bd3.png" style="width:133px;"/>
                          </a>
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right" style="max-width:500px;">
                     <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                      <noscript>
                      </noscript>
                      <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-105025103717" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                       <div class="body read-more-cut">
                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <p>
                          <em>
                           <img alt="Dad Faces 20 Years for Cheating Harvard Financial Aid" height="507" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w338/2ecf3d33d72bcc050f4e05d299c9dcf2ae09454d.jpg" width="338"/>
                          </em>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <em>
                           Harvard University, Cambridge, Massachusetts. Photo: Coleong/Thinkstock
                          </em>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The College Board recently
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:3692d62e-e626-3217-821c-8230d2a0d04f;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.usnews.com/news/articles/2013/10/23/charts-just-how-fast-has-college-tuition-grown" target="_blank">
                           reported
                          </a>
                          that college costs are
                          <em>
                           finally
                          </em>
                          decelerating  tuition grew just 2.9 percent this year versus the roughly 7 percent its been growing each year for
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:3692d62e-e626-3217-821c-8230d2a0d04f;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.forbes.com/sites/steveodland/2012/03/24/college-costs-are-soaring/" target="_blank">
                           decades
                          </a>
                          . But theyre still growing faster than household incomes, creating a desperate situation for many parents  including, apparently, the dad of a
                          <span>
                           former Harvard University student, who admitted
                          </span>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:3692d62e-e626-3217-821c-8230d2a0d04f;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.bostonglobe.com/metro/2014/12/11/man-falsifies-records-daughter-can-awarded-financial-aid-from-harvard-university/qyzFXrG4ImuIdXwjDgzlVL/story.html?p1=Article_Trending_Most_Viewed" target="_blank">
                           Tuesday
                          </a>
                          <span>
                           that he resorted to lying to get his daughters financial aid. He now he faces up to 20 years in prison for the deception.
                          </span>
                          <br/>
                          <br/>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:3692d62e-e626-3217-821c-8230d2a0d04f;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.yahoo.com/parenting/parents-of-valedictorians-howd-you-do-that-99923334887.html" target="_blank">
                           <em>
                            <strong>
                             STORY: Secrets From Parents of Valedictorians
                            </strong>
                           </em>
                          </a>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Joseph N. Fonge pleaded guilty in U.S. District Court in Boston to three counts of wire fraud for falsifying his income. The changes he made scored his daughter more than $160,000 in financial aid from the university and the federal government over three years. (For context, the national average for undergrad financial aid was
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:3692d62e-e626-3217-821c-8230d2a0d04f;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.insidehighered.com/news/2014/11/13/report-shows-slowdown-tuition-increases-education-borrowing" target="_blank">
                           $14,180
                          </a>
                          per full-time student last year.)
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:3692d62e-e626-3217-821c-8230d2a0d04f;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.yahoo.com/parenting/dad-speaks-out-after-21-year-old-sues-him-to-pay-104864515872.html" target="_blank">
                           <em>
                            <strong>
                             STORY:Dad Speaks Out After 21-Year-Old Sues Him to Pay College Tuition
                            </strong>
                           </em>
                          </a>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The fathers inaccurate federal income tax returns misrepresented the students need in the College Scholarship Service profile and Free Application for Federal Student Aid (FAFSA) for tuition help at Harvard, where
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:3692d62e-e626-3217-821c-8230d2a0d04f;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://college.harvard.edu/financial-aid/how-aid-works/cost-attendance" target="_blank">
                           70 percent
                          </a>
                          of attendees get financial aid to cover the $58,607yearly cost.And thats not all: Fonge is also on the hook for defrauding the University of Rochester $46,600 for another daughter back in 2010. He is scheduled to be sentenced March 4.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          But this fraud doesnt surprise college planning expert Bev Taylor. Falsifying documents regarding college applications is no big news these days, t
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:3692d62e-e626-3217-821c-8230d2a0d04f;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://theivycoach.com/" target="_blank">
                           he Ivy Coach
                          </a>
                          tells Yahoo Parenting. Kids are falsifying documents all the time, cheating on the SATs and such.
                          <br/>
                          <br/>
                          Ditto, says student financial aid expert,
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:3692d62e-e626-3217-821c-8230d2a0d04f;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.kantrowitz.com/kantrowitz/mark.html" target="_blank">
                           Mark Kantrowitz
                          </a>
                          , who literally wrote the book on the aid process, called
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:3692d62e-e626-3217-821c-8230d2a0d04f;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0991464605/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=211189&amp;creative=373489&amp;creativeASIN=0991464605&amp;link_code=as3&amp;tag=cancerpoints-20" target="_blank">
                           <em>
                            Filling the FAFSA
                           </em>
                          </a>
                          . I see stories every couple of weeks with someone convicted of financial aid fraud, but the amounts tend to be relatively small, so unless its a ring or theres something sensationalistic about it, it doesnt get much attention. Scamming for federal Pell grants is most common, says Kantrowitz. Indeed, the U.S. Deptartment of Education
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:3692d62e-e626-3217-821c-8230d2a0d04f;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/robert-siciliano/student-financial-aid-fra_b_4713385.html" target="_blank">
                           flagged
                          </a>
                          126,000 suspect applicants for the 2013-2014 school year.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          With about $150 billion in federal grants, loans, and work study given out by the
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:3692d62e-e626-3217-821c-8230d2a0d04f;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.ed.gov/" target="_blank">
                           U.S. Department of Education
                          </a>
                          in 2013 alone, per spokeswoman Jane Glickman, theres a lot of money up for grabs.
                          <br/>
                          <br/>
                          In recent years, the agency has gotten stricter, about how students and parents file for aid, says Kantrowitz. They are now requiring that information come directly from the IRS instead of the individuals, for instance, and cracking down on fraud withindependent audits, inspections, and other reviews conducted
                          <span>
                           by the law enforcement arm of the department, the
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:3692d62e-e626-3217-821c-8230d2a0d04f;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www2.ed.gov/about/offices/list/oig/index.html" target="_blank">
                            Office of Inspector General
                           </a>
                          </span>
                          <span>
                           .
                          </span>
                          "Investigating and fighting student aid fraud has long been a top priority of our office," theirPublic Affairs Liaison Catherine Grant tells Yahoo Parenting.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Schools dont take the matter lightly, either. Some universities will expel a student who commits financial fraud  even if it was the parent who falsified the documents, according to Kantrowitz. The student signed them. So parents really need to know: If you commit fraud on the FAFSA, besides stealing from the federal government, youre putting yourself and your kids at risk.
                         </p>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:999999px;max-width:500px;">
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>

                   <div class="Font-A-4-110 Pb-20">
                    What to Read Next
                   </div>
                   <div class="height-truncater Ov-h">

                     <div class="item Td-n Pos-r D-b Ov-h SlowTrans has-image" id="article-aft-image-link-105025103717-124088241017" style="padding:0 0 40px;">
                      <a data-action-outcome="open" data-routable-url="/parenting/1/lightning-strikes-mom-holding-2-year-old-124088241017.html" data-ylk="g:c5b10cd5-e0bb-3999-8fd2-9dbcd49dd39f;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:also;ad:0;cpos:1;itc:0;t8:tileview;t9:21;elm:img;elmt:ct;" href="/parenting/lightning-strikes-mom-holding-2-year-old-124088241017.html" style="color:#000;">
                       <span class="item-image Pos-r Fl-start Mend-20 Ov-h" style="background-image:none;height:125.77142857142859px;width:155px;">
                        <img class="ImageLoader Pos-a Start-0" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" style="width:155px;height:auto;left:50%;margin-left:-77.5px;top:50%;margin-top:-62.88571428571429px;background-image:url(https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w175/88b5c09836226a9746ed2d68fa6a0dc5551e1ebf.jpg);"/>
                       </span>
                      </a>

root.App.Cache.genUrl = function (routeName, context) {
        var route = routeMap[routeName],
            path, keys, i, len, key, param, regex;

        if (!route) { return ''; }

        path = route.path;
        keys = route.keys;

        if (context &amp;&amp; (len = keys.length)) {
            for (i = 0; i &lt; len; i += 1) {
                key   = keys[i];
                param = key.name || key;
                regex = new RegExp('[:*]' + param + '\\b');
                path  = path.replace(regex, context[param]);
            }
        }

        // Replace missing params with empty strings.
        return path.replace(/([:*])([\w\-]+)?/g, '');
    };

(Photo: Center For Medical Progress)&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EA new&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=jjxwVuozMnU\"\u003Evideo\u003C\u002Fa\u003E showing a top-level Planned Parenthood official supposedly discussing the sale of body parts of aborted fetuses has put abortion back in the headlines today, particularly in conservative outlets.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe eight-minute clip features Dr. Deborah Nucatola, Planned Parenthood&#x2019;s senior director of medical services, at what appears to be a routine business lunch. But the unseen people at her table inquiring about fetal organs are actually investigators posing as members of a fetal-tissue procurement company.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003ESTORY:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fparenting\u002Fa-new-reminder-that-pro-choice-is-not-121775317302.html\"\u003EA New Reminder That &#x201C;Pro-Choice&#x201D; Is Not &#x201C;Anti-Baby&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFilmed and released by a Calif.-based organization called the&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.centerformedicalprogress.org\u002F\"\u003ECenter for Medical Progress\u003C\u002Fa\u003E (CMP), the footage implies that Planned Parenthood violates federal law by selling fetal tissue, a felony punishable by up to 10 years in prison.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPlanned Parenthood strongly denies the accusation. In a statement released to Yahoo Parenting, Eric Ferrero, vice president of communications, notes that Planned Parenthood donates fetal tissue &#x201C;to scientific research that can help lead to medical breakthroughs,&#x201D; which is not illegal. &#x201C;There is no financial benefit for tissue donation for either the patient or Planned Parenthood,&#x201D; the statement continues.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003ESTORY:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fparenting\u002Fabortion-rights-leader-is-pregnant-and-her-121121545742.html\"\u003EAbortion Rights Leader Is Pregnant &#x2014; and Her Critics Are Appalled&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe conversation on the video clip (released by CMP in long form on \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=H4UjIM9B9KQ\"\u003EYouTube\u003C\u002Fa\u003E), can be graphic. When one of the &#x201C;investigators&#x201D; asks about prices, Nucatola replies, &#x201C;You know, I would throw a number out, I would say it&#x2019;s probably anywhere from $30 to $100, depending on the facility and what&#x2019;s involved.&#x201D; The fake rep then clarifies, &#x201C;The $30 to $100 price range, that&#x2019;s per specimen that we&#x2019;re talking about, right?&#x201D; Nucatola answers, &#x201C;Per specimen. Yes.&#x201D;&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPlanned Parenthood states that the &#x201C;price range&#x201D; refers to the cost to donate tissue. &#x201C;At several of our health centers, we help patients who want to donate tissue for scientific research, and we do this just like every other high-quality health care provider does &#x2014; with full, appropriate consent from patients and under the highest ethical and legal standards,&#x201D; Ferrero notes. &#x201C;In some instances, actual costs, such as the cost to transport tissue to leading research centers, are reimbursed, which is standard across the medical field.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ERepresentatives from CMP did not respond to Yahoo Parenting&#x2019;s request for comment. On the organization&#x2019;s website, which was down for much of the afternoon on Tuesday, CMP identifies itself a collection of &#x201C;citizen journalists dedicated to monitoring and reporting on medical ethics and advances. We are concerned about contemporary bioethical issues that impact human dignity, and we oppose any interventions, procedures, and experiments that exploit the unequal legal status of any class of human beings.&#x201D;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut Planned Parenthood further explains that the accusation of selling fetal body parts is old and unfounded, and that CMP has clear ulterior motives, noting, &#x201C;The promotional video mischaracterizing Planned Parenthood&#x2019;s mission and services is made by a long time anti-abortion activist that has used deceptive and unethical video editing, and that has created a fake medical website as well as a fake human tissue website that purports to provide services to stem cell researchers.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe statement continues, &#x201C;Similar false accusations have been put forth by opponents of abortion services for decades. These groups have been widely discredited and their claims fall apart on closer examination, just as they do in this case.&#x201D;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPlease follow @YahooParenting on \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ffacebook.com\u002Fyahooparenting\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EFacebook\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E, \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftwitter.com\u002Fyahooparenting\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003ETwitter\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E, \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Finstagram.com\u002Fyahooparenting\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EInstagram\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E, and&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.pinterest.com\u002Fyahoo\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPinterest\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E. Strikes Mom Holding 2-Year-Old","summary":"A New Hampshire mother and her 2-year-old son who were struck by lightning last week have come out of the incident with their lives src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F80f17dce289a3394143ca61e10e8b0ee32ec3135.jpg\" alt=\"Lightning Strikes Mom Holding 2-Year-Old\" width=\"540\" height=\"307\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EKelly Bell and her son, Logan (being held by his father, Dan Bell) survived a lightning strike. (Photo: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wmur.com\u002Fnews\u002Fmarlborough-mother-and-toddler-recovering-after-being-struck-by-lightning\u002F34126072\"\u003EWMUR\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EA New Hampshire mother and her 2-year-old son who \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wmur.com\u002Fnews\u002Fmarlborough-mother-and-toddler-recovering-after-being-struck-by-lightning\u002F34126072\"\u003Ewere struck by lightning\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;last week have lived to tell about the incident. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOn Tuesday, Kelly Bell and her son Logan headed outside after a thunderstorm, but it turned out the weather wasn&#x2019;t quite over. &#x201C;I thought the thunder had passed, it had been 30 minutes since we&#x2019;d seen anything, so we went outside to see the rain because we like to look at it,&#x201D; Bell tells Yahoo Parenting. &#x201C;I said &#x2018;Hey Bubba, look at the rain,&#x2019; and then next thing I knew I woke up on the floor.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003ESTORY:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fparenting\u002Fboy-suffers-severe-injury-on-playground-slide-122351703687.html\"\u003EBoy Suffers &#x2018;Severe&#x2019; Injury on Playground Slide: What Parents Need to Know\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBell says the lightning struck a tree, and then traveled along a metal dog lead, which was connected from the tree to their porch. &#x201C;We weren&#x2019;t touching anything, just standing on the porch,&#x201D; she says. &#x201C;The lightning struck the tree, and traveled into the dog lead, which was attached to a nail under our porch. My hand was probably six to eight inches from the lead and the best we can guess is that the lightning traveled into my hand through my wedding ring.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"507\" height=\"760\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w507\u002Fcfea93c171bde2d7012d774272b36cec24c0e355.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EKelly Bell standing next to the tree that was struck by lightning before the electricity traveled to strike Bell and her son. (Photo:&#xA0;Bill Gnade\u002FKeene Sentinel)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESince Bell was holding Logan, he was affected too, although Bell bore the brunt of the impact. &#x201C;He was on my right side and I was struck on my left,&#x201D; she says. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBoth mother and son suffered injuries: Logan has bruises and burns, while Bell was left deaf in one ear. &#x201C;It may or may not be permanent damage,&#x201D; she says. &#x201C;There&#x2019;s a hole that takes up about a third of my eardrum, so it&#x2019;s a waiting game to see if my hearing will improve.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003ESTORY:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fparenting\u002Fwhat-every-kid-should-know-about-safety-by-age-6-119613668012.html\"\u003EWhat Every Kid Should Know About Safety By Age 6\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELogan is already on the mend. &#x201C;Most of his bruises are just about gone, he&#x2019;s back to being his old self,&#x201D; she says. &#x201C;He still likes to go outside, and he&#x2019;s not afraid of the porch so that&#x2019;s good. But we haven&#x2019;t had any more thunderstorms yet.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBell&#x2019;s doctors say it could have been much worse, and that the mother is extremely lucky. Still, she&#x2019;s not sure she sees it that way. &#x201C;Lucky would have been had we stayed inside and the lightning struck and didn&#x2019;t hit us, but I&#x2019;m happy to be here,&#x201D; she says.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDr. Deborah Gilboa, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Faskdoctorg.com\u002F\"\u003Ea Pittsburgh-based parenting expert and family physician\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, says lightning strikes can certainly be fatal. &#x201C;Electricity passes from where it touches you to the ground, and it is looking for the most direct route to the ground, so if that is through your heart, it can kill you,&#x201D; she tells Yahoo Parenting. &#x201C;It will affect you and whoever you are holding hands with or, in this case, holding.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf you live in a particularly susceptible area, you may want to look into lightning rods to protect your home, Gilboa says. &#x201C;Keep in mind that lightning is, for the most part, drawn to the tallest thing in the area,&#x201D; she says. To protect your family from harm, you should keep your family indoors throughout a storm, and steer clear of anything that might easily draw a lightning strike, like telephone poles or tall trees. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAs for the Bell family, they are facing a number of medical bills, and Bell says she does not have medical insurance. In order to cover the cost of the ambulance and hospital bills, she has started a \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.gofundme.com\u002Fyw27cc\"\u003EGoFundMe page\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. &#x201C;My wonderful husband won&#x2019;t leave our side which means we are going to have very little to no money coming in while we heal since he is the only one who works,&#x201D; Bell explains on the page. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMoving forward, Bell says she will be watching rainstorms from inside. &#x201C;Even if you think the weather has passed, if it still looks storming and it is still raining, stay inside,&#x201D; she says. &#x201C;Lightning can be in the area, and you have no idea.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s a lesson Bell had to learn the hard way, but as she points out, &#x201C;I&#x2019;m just glad we&#x2019;re here to have learned the lesson at all.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPlease follow @YahooParenting on \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ffacebook.com\u002Fyahooparenting\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EFacebook\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E, \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftwitter.com\u002Fyahooparenting\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003ETwitter\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E, \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Finstagram.com\u002Fyahooparenting\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EInstagram\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E, and \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.pinterest.com\u002Fyahoo\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPinterest\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E. &#x201C;Does anyone know a family who would like to adopt a 4 year old girl?&#x201D;&#xA0;(Photo: Stocksy)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EA family in Dubuque, Iowa was reportedly investigated by police recently after a member of the clan &#x2014; whose name has been withheld in the local news story &#x2014; wrote a post on Facebook that offered up their 4-year-old for adoption.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I need some help,&#x201D; began her note, posted over the weekend to the private, 4,000-member DBQ Mamas group in Dubuque and re-published Monday on \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.kwwl.com\u002Fstory\u002F29538368\u002F2015\u002F07\u002F13\u002Ffacebook-post-offering-4-year-old-for-adoption-investigated\"\u003EKWWL\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. &#x201C;Does anyone know a family who would like to adopt a 4 year old girl. My parents adopted her but got new jobs and they have no time for her. I have 3 kids of my own and can not handle another. Serious inquiries only.&#x201C;&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003ESTORY\u003C\u002Fb\u003E:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fparenting\u002Fman-reunites-with-siblings-after-40-years-123379643667.html\"\u003EMan Reunites With Siblings After 40 Years, Discovers They&#x2019;d Met Before\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EKWWL reports that Dubuque Police Lt. Scott Baxter said his department got &#x201C;several calls&#x201D; about the post and dispatched an officer to investigate. &#x201C;We determined no criminal act had been committed and there was not sufficient probable cause to warrant an arrest or charge,&#x201D; Baxter tells Yahoo Parenting. &#x201C;The welfare of the 4-year-old was checked and determined satisfactory. To my knowledge, the 4-year-old remained with the adopted parents referenced by the person who made the post.&#x201D; Baxter adds that the police department notified the Department of Human Services about the post on Facebook. &#x201C;Obviously the post was not well thought out, as so many aren&#x2019;t on social media,&#x201D; he says.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003ESTORY\u003C\u002Fb\u003E:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fparenting\u002Ftwo-dads-adopt-their-seventh-child-a-gay-teen-121781515352.html\"\u003ETwo Dads Adopt Their Seventh Child, a Gay Teen\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn a later post (\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fdbqkidsguide.com\u002Fthink-before-you-post-statement-from-the-admins-dbq-mamas-facebook-group\u002F\"\u003Eremoved by DBQ Mamas administrators\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, as was&#xA0;the original note, after law enforcement got involved), the woman appeared to backpedal on her intent to re-home the preschooler via social media. &quot;Let me rephrase,&#x201D; she wrote, according to KWWL, &#x201C;I&#x2019;m not selling a kid, it was to help find adoption ideas. So calling the police to receive suggestions was ridiculous. She&#x2019;s safe and fine. So thank you for your help.&quot;&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut upset about the incident has yet to die down in Dubuque &#x2014; or in the larger adoption community.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHundreds of commenters forwarded and posted notes in response to KWWL&#x2019;s \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.facebook.com\u002FKWWL7\u002Fposts\u002F10153519096606528\"\u003Earticle about the incident on Facebook\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, where remarks ran the gamut from outrage to pity &#x2014; for everyone involved. &#x201C;Children are not objects you get then discard when you just don&#x2019;t have the time,&#x201D; fumed one commenter. &#x201C;YOU BE A RESPONSIBLE ADULT AND MAKE TIME.&#x201D; Another commenter joined others urging critics to reserve their judgment. &#x201C;While it&#x2019;s extremely sad that someone is giving up a child maybe they are trying to give the child a better life, maybe that&#x2019;s the absolute best thing that they can do.&#x201D;&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s not clear in this case whether or not re-homing &#x2014; the process of moving an adopted child to another home &#x2014; was at play. And it is something that&#x2019;s &#x201C;not common, thank goodness,&#x201D; Adam Pertman, President of the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.nationalcenteronadoptionandpermanency.net\u002F\"\u003ENational Center on Adoption and Permanency\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;tells Yahoo Parenting. &#x201C;But it does happen, and it usually happens because a parent doesn&#x2019;t know what else to do. It&#x2019;s not jettisoning a kid because they didn&#x2019;t do their homework. It&#x2019;s that something awful is happening and the parents don&#x2019;t know where to turn. Typically it&#x2019;s after they&#x2019;ve tried everything and just want to help the child get parented properly.&#x201D;&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPertman is quick to say that he doesn&#x2019;t defend the behavior. &#x201C;Adoption is not supposed to be child rental; If things don&#x2019;t work out, you return the product,&#x201D; says the \u003Ci\u003EAdoption Nation\u003C\u002Fi\u003E author. But he acknowledges that the ultimate goal should always be to provide what&#x2019;s best for the child. &#x201C;This is not the way to respond to crisis &#x2014; posting on Facebook because you can &#x2014; but people who are stressed and don&#x2019;t know what to do make mistakes.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EInstead of simply vilifying the parents trying to re-home adopted kids, Pertman urges people to instead respond to stories like this with a focus on how we can provide whatever it is that families need to keep whole, whether it be legal support, social services help, or community assistance. &#x201C;The message in nearly all of these cases is that we&#x2019;re not doing enough to help families deal with their issues and succeed,&#x201D; he says. &#x201C;Most people think, &#x2018;Oh look at those terrible parents,&#x2019; but we know from examples we have seen that they&#x2019;re not terrible people, they&#x2019;re people at their wits&#x2019; end and don&#x2019;t know what to do to help their children.&#x201D; And it&#x2019;s something that we, as a country, need to figure out, says Pertman. &#x201C;We&#x2019;re talking about very big stakes: It&#x2019;s a child&#x2019;s life.&#x201D;&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPlease follow @YahooParenting on \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ffacebook.com\u002Fyahooparenting\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EFacebook\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E, \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftwitter.com\u002Fyahooparenting\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003ETwitter\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E, \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Finstagram.com\u002Fyahooparenting\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EInstagram\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E, and \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.pinterest.com\u002Fyahoo\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPinterest\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E. (Photo: Yahoo Parenting)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EA \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.facebook.com\u002Fbfmamatalk\u002Fphotos\u002Fa.471668436214912.96317.411182815596808\u002F889891364392615\u002F?type=1&amp;theater\"\u003Ephoto of a notice to Target employees\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which spells out the store&#x2019;s breastfeeding policies, is going viral this week, with many mothers applauding the company&#x2019;s explicit instructions to make nursing mothers feel welcome.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E The photo was posted to the mother&#x2019;s group \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.facebook.com\u002Fbfmamatalk?fref=photo\"\u003EBreastfeeding Mama Talk&#x2019;s Facebook page\u003C\u002Fa\u003E on Sunday, and has since been shared more than 15,500 times and received nearly 40,000 likes. The instructions to employees that are featured in the photo state: \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Guests may openly breastfeed in our stores or ask where they can go to breastfeed their child. When this happens, remember these points. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cul\u003E \n \u003Cli\u003E- Target&#x2019;s policy supports breastfeeding in any area of our stores, including our fitting rooms, even if others are waiting. \u003C\u002Fli\u003E \n \u003Cli\u003E- If you see a woman breastfeeding in our stores, do not approach her. \u003C\u002Fli\u003E \n \u003Cli\u003E- If she approaches you and asks for a location to breastfeed, offer the fitting room (do not offer the restroom as an option)&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fli\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"371\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F8803c9df6a56aa4ad4bbbe709db3f4daca16da52.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThis sign, which spells out Target&#x2019;s breastfeeding policy, has gone viral on Facebook. (Photo: Facebook\u002FBreastfeeding Mama Talk)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003ESTORY:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fparenting\u002Fmom-donates-38-gallons-of-breast-milk-worth-123738270082.html\"\u003EMom Donates 38 Gallons of Breast Milk &#x2014; Worth $29K! &#x2014; For a Good Cause\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn a caption to the photo, Breastfeeding Mama Talk wrote &#x201C;Kudos to Target for their breastfeeding friendly policy. Other businesses should take note. Please share this everywhere especially on the Facebook pages of the businesses known to discriminate against breastfeeding!&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EComments poured in, celebrating Target&#x2019;s family-friendly policy. &#x201C;Good work to them for getting it right and training their staff properly on this, especially love &#x2018;do not offer the restroom as an option.&#x2019; So many other places have been guilty of this!!&#x201D; wrote one user.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAnother frequent shopper wrote, &#x201C;I&#x2019;ve nursed at Target in the fitting rooms and just walking around the store. Never got a comment or even side-eyed. &#x2026; I will always be a Target customer!&#x201D; Another satisfied mom chimed in that she had seen the policies in action: &#x201C;About a month ago I was nursing my daughter and a customer went and got a manager, brought them to where I was nursing (in the men&#x2019;s section with my husband, covered up) and complained. The manager apologized to me and explained to the LADY that I was allowed to feed my baby wherever I am comfortable doing so. And proceeded to explain to the lady that if she didn&#x2019;t like it, don&#x2019;t watch.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003ESTORY:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fparenting\u002Fmom-calls-out-breastfeeding-shamer-on-facebook-120447787867.html\"\u003EMom Calls Out Breastfeeding Shamer on Facebook\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe policies extend to employees, said one commenter. &#x201C;I used to work for Target,&#x201D; she said. &#x201C;It wasn&#x2019;t just for the guests, they even had a special mommy room for breastfeeding employees. [There] was a fridge, rocking chair, radio, the whole nine yards. It was amazing.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe positive feedback is a nice change of pace for Target, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.cbsnews.com\u002Fnews\u002Fbreastfeeding-moms-stage-nurse-in-protests-at-target-stores\u002F\"\u003Ewhich came under fire in 2011\u003C\u002Fa\u003E when a Texas mom said she was harassed for breastfeeding her son in the store. She claimed that several employees asked her to relocate from the floor to a fitting room, and one implied that she could be cited for indecent exposure. After calling customer relations to complain, that mother said she was told, &#x201C;Just because it&#x2019;s a woman&#x2019;s legal right to nurse a baby in public doesn&#x2019;t mean she should walk around the store flaunting it.&#x201D; In response, breastfeeding moms organized a nurse-in at 100 Target stores around the country. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAt the time, Target responded that it supports breastfeeding in stores, and the company would work to better educate employees about the store&#x2019;s policies. If the recent Facebook photo is to be believed, it has done just that. &#x201C;At Target, we want all of our guests to feel comfortable shopping with us,&#x201D; a Target spokesperson told Yahoo Parenting. &#x201C;Our breastfeeding policy, which applies to all stores, is just one of the ways in which we support our guests.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EDiana West, director of media relations for \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.llli.org\u002F\"\u003ELa Leche League International\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, says the photo is a great example of a company taking a proactive approach to educate employees. &#x201C;This way there is no confusion about any policies about the rights of a breastfeeding mother,&#x201D; she tells Yahoo Parenting. &#x201C;It&#x2019;s also reassurance to breastfeeding moms that they have the backing of the company, so that they can be confident customers and know they will be supported in the stores.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe policy, and the attention it&#x2019;s getting, is especially important right now, as a number of stores are coming under fire for poor treatment of nursing moms. On Monday, a \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.huffingtonpost.co.uk\u002F2015\u002F07\u002F14\u002Fprimark-investigates-allegations-security-guard-breastfeeding-baby-nursing-mother_n_7791618.html?ir=UK+Parents&amp;ncid=tweetlnkushpmg00000067\"\u003Emother in England claimed\u003C\u002Fa\u003E that a security guard asked her to vacate the premises of a Primark clothing store because she was breastfeeding. Caroline Starmer \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.facebook.com\u002Ffreetofeeduk\u002Fposts\u002F417574848429242\"\u003Eposted on the breastfeeding group Free to Feed&#x2019;s Facebook page\u003C\u002Fa\u003E that when she refused to leave, the security guard physically removed her daughter from her breast and walked away with the baby girl. Today, Primark \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.huffingtonpost.co.uk\u002F2015\u002F07\u002F14\u002Fprimark--cctv-shows-no-evidence-nursing-mothers-child-snatched-breast-_n_7792962.html?1436880982\"\u003Edenied the incident\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and issued a statement saying, &#x201C;We have investigated this customer&#x2019;s allegation which we naturally take very seriously indeed,&#x201D; according to the \u003Ci\u003EHuffington Post\u003C\u002Fi\u003E. &#x201C;The [security] footage, reviewed by store management, shows the customer in the Leicester store quite clearly during the time in question. We can see no evidence that she was approached by anyone during this period.&#x201D; The statement goes on to say that security guards deny the allegations, and that Primark supports breastfeeding mothers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ELast year, a nursing mom in a Texas Victoria&#x2019;s Secret claimed that she asked a sales clerk about using a fitting room to nurse and was told she could &#x201C;walk outside to a nearby alley,&#x201D; according to \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Faustin.culturemap.com\u002Fnews\u002Fcity-life\u002F01-17-14-victorias-secret-breast-feeding-denied-domain\u002F\"\u003EAustin CultureMap\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. And at an Oklahoma Walmart in February, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.fox23.com\u002Fnews\u002Fnews\u002Flocal\u002Fbreastfeeding-moms-hold-nurse-glenpool-walmart\u002Fnj4MD\u002F\"\u003Emoms held a nurse-in\u003C\u002Fa\u003E after one woman said she was asked not to breastfeed in the store. Both companies responded publicly to the claims stating that they welcome breastfeeding mothers. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWest says that oftentimes these problems arise because store employees simple aren&#x2019;t aware of the policies. &#x201C;This is what they are trying to fix,&#x201D; she says. &#x201C;Employees sometimes feel uncomfortable, because they don&#x2019;t know what to say and don&#x2019;t want to get in trouble for saying or doing the wrong thing. This way, they will be educated, and they can do the right thing for the company and for the shoppers.&#x201D; Other stores, West notes, would do well to follow suit and set clear policies and communicate those policies to employees. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EJake Marcus, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.jakemarcus.com\u002F\"\u003Ea Philadelphia attorney and expert in breastfeeding law\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, says the sign is a step in the right direction, but could do better. &#x201C;On the one hand, it says guests may openly breastfeed, but on the other hand, it says if you are asked a location, offer the fitting room,&#x201D; she tells Yahoo Parenting. &#x201C;If I were a not-well-informed employee of Target, I could interpret this as requiring women to breastfeed in fitting rooms only.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EStill, Marcus says the sign is well-intended, if perhaps poorly written. &#x201C;I foresee more than a few employees saying you can only do this in the fitting room, which is not the intent,&#x201D; she points out. &#x201C;I think what they are trying to say is that women can breastfeed anywhere and don&#x2019;t mess with them. And that&#x2019;s the way it should be, and the way employees should behave in all states.&#x201D; Her hope, she says, is that Target conducts employee training to help enforce its policy. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAs for the viral nature of the photo, West says mothers have been waiting a long time for this sort of acknowledgement. &#x201C;It&#x2019;s a nerve-wracking thing for a mother to do what she needs to do for her family &#x2013; go shopping, do errands &#x2013; and also feed her baby. It&#x2019;s especially hard for someone who isn&#x2019;t used to doing so in public. This is a company that is saying &#x2018;this is a safe zone, you won&#x2019;t be harassed.&#x2019; Breastfeeding mothers have been waiting for this kind of support for a long time, and it&#x2019;s a beautiful thing.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPlease follow @YahooParenting on \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ffacebook.com\u002Fyahooparenting\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EFacebook\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E, \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftwitter.com\u002Fyahooparenting\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003ETwitter\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E, \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Finstagram.com\u002Fyahooparenting\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EInstagram\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E, and \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.pinterest.com\u002Fyahoo\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPinterest\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E. O'Neill","title":"Writer","bio":"Jennifer ONeill has two children but isnt a minivan mom -- yet.
